SMS Code Provisioning Guidelines
Use a Mexico short code for alphanumeric codes one-way sends. You can register up to 7 alphanumeric
codes. Network carriers must approve and allowlist all alphanumeric codes before deployment. These
codes must have a minimum of 3 and a maximum of 11 alphanumeric characters.
You can also use short codes for two-way sends marketing and transactional sends, but not all network
carriers support these sends.
Network carriers require monthly sending rates of at least 100,000 sends per month to keep a short code
active. We recommend planning your sending rate as soon as possible before procuring a short code.
Conduct marketing sends from Monday through Friday, 9 AM to 8 PM (UTC−03:00 or -04:00, depending
on the season).

SMS Code Provisioning Guidelines
When sending one-way messages, use an alphanumeric code for Peru's private short code owners, and a
Peru short code for two-way messaging. Alphanumeric code registration is reserved for local enterprises
only, meaning businesses with headquarters in Peru. Local carriers must approve all alphanumeric code

maximum of 11 characters.

Important Due to increased spam and fraud, two-way support on PH long codes is no longer
available. Local long codes now only support inbound (MO) SMS. All outbound (MT) messages from
numeric long codes are blocked. Therefore, conversational use cases aren't supported. While long
codes can still receive STOP and HELP requests, the system can’t send a confirmation text response.

to-action message by using the local long code number in the alphanumeric sends.

ownership, and trademark certificates for alphanumeric sender IDs that differ from your enterprise
name.

All messages must contain your company, brand, or service name at the beginning of that message.

any trademark certificates. Print all letters on corporate letterhead, then sign, date, and rubber-stamp
them.

alphanumeric codes don't need to register URLs. Domains in the URL must be associated with the
enterprise, brand, product, or service. Register each URL and domain and make sure it's working so they
can be validated.

Unified Messaging Unified Messaging Setup
preregistration preregistration preregistration
SMS Code Provisioning Guidelines
Use a Singapore alphanumeric code for sending one-way messages, both locally and internationally. Use
a Singapore long or short code for two-way messaging.
Alphanumeric codes can't be generic. They must be associated with a brand, enterprise, product, or
service. These codes can only use alphanumeric characters and spaces, with a minimum of 3 and a
maximum of 11 characters.
To make sure your SMS messages to Singapore aren't labeled as Likely Scam or blocked, register your
alphanumeric code or preallocated short or long code in the SMS Sender ID Registry (SSIR) Portal. To
register the code, follow the instructions in the SSIR Guide. For all codes, add Sinch Singapore Pte Ltd as
the SMS aggregator or supplier. For long codes, provide the phone number without the 65 country code
prefix. For example, register the number 6598233122 as 98233122. For details, see the SSIR rules of
registration.
After your code is approved, complete the Singapore Letter of Authorisation (LOA) and share it with your
Salesforce account executive.
Even if your business isn’t based in Singapore, you can sign up on the SSIR Portal after you get a local
Unique Entity Number (UEN). You can obtain a UEN by registering with the Accounting and Corporate
Regulatory Authority (ACRA). Register as a local subsidiary or foreign branch office, after paying the
required fees.
Restricted Content
You’re responsible for complying with local rules and regulations. To ensure compliance, familiarize
yourself with the legislation of the local market. Provide an opt-out option in marketing messages and
communicate during business hours only. Make sure your contact lists exclude numbers listed in the
national Do Not Call (DNC) Registry or establish explicit consent before sending messages. The Monetary
Authority of Singapore (MAS) and the Association of Banks in Singapore (ABS) have enhanced digital
banking security by removing clickable links in SMS messages. Therefore, all financial institutions must
omit links in their SMS communications. Singapore generally forbids content related, but not limited to,
adult, drugs, tobacco, money lending, and gambling products and services.
Best Practices and Compliance References
Consider using different alphanumeric codes for marketing and transactional messaging.
Telecommunications in Singapore are regulated by these organizations:
•
Infocomm Media Development Authority (IMDA)
•
Government Technology Agency (GovTech)
•
Personal Data Protection Commission (PDPC)

Make sure that your US short code supports MMS. A short code that supports MMS automatically

should always verify the code capabilities before you launch a campaign.
Messaging Requirements
Use a call to action to engage your users. For example, send a prompt to a user to opt in to receive offers
or enter a contest.
A call to action must include:
•
Program name
232

=== PAGE 237 ===
Unified Messaging Unified Messaging Setup
•
Message frequency
•
Link to customer terms and conditions with privacy policy and help information
Terms and conditions must include:
•
“Text STOP to stop,” including bold STOP
•
“Text HELP for help,” including bold HELP
•
A description of how the user opts in
•
How the call to action is delivered. For example: web, in-store signage
Note If you send a web form, text boxes can’t be pre-checked.
•
An opt-in keyword that, if not a web form, must be in bold
•
Screenshots of the call to action and message flow
Limitations in Unicode Support
Unicode encoding is supported for SMS messages in the US, but there are some limitations.
•
Reduced character count—Unicode (UCS-2) encoding allows you send only 70 characters per message.
•
Concatenation impact—Multi-part Unicode messages use more segments. For example, a
160-character message is split into three parts.
•
Carrier filtering—Some US carriers may filter, truncate, or fail to deliver messages if Unicode isn't used
properly. Unicode-heavy content might also trigger spam filters.
•
Unreliable delivery receipts—Delivery receipts may be unreliable with Unicode characters, especially
when using 10DLC or shared short codes.
Use Unicode only when necessary, such as for names or text in non-Latin scripts. Keep messages short to
avoid excessive segmentation. Avoid using emojis in critical alerts or regulatory messages. Use Unicode
carefully because of the reduced message length and potential delivery issues. For critical
communications, opt for GSM-7 encoding whenever possible.
Restricted Content
Carriers can restrict messaging with the listed content:
•
Content related to sex, hate, alcohol, firearms, and tobacco (SHAFT)
•
Content relating to illegal substances, including cannabis and cannabis-related products, such as
cannabidiol (CBD), vaping products or devices, marijuana or cannabis, or dispensaries
•
SPAM, fraud, phishing
•
Lead-generation programs
•
Deceptive programs
•
High-risk financial services, such as payday loans, short-term loans, third-party home and auto loans,
student loans, and debt collection
•
Debt forgiveness, debt consolidation, debt reduction, and credit repair programs
•
Illegal prescriptions or drug endorsements
•
Work and investment opportunities, such as work-from-home programs, job alerts from third-party
233

=== PAGE 238 ===
Unified Messaging Unified Messaging Setup
recruiting firms, and risk investment opportunities
•
Carrier competitive promotions
•
Fraudulent or misleading messages
•
Gambling
•
Profanity
•
Depictions or endorsement of violence
•
Lead generation indicating the sharing of collected information with third parties
•
Short code programs that solicit charitable or political donations that don’t comply with Cellular
Telecommunications and Internet Association (CTIA) best practices.
•
Abandoned shopping cart notifications without applicable consent
•
Campaign types not in compliance with the Messaging Principles and Best Practices, CTIA Short Code
Monitoring Handbook, and any other legal regulatory body governing telecommunication systems in
this country
Short Code Audits
The CTIA conducts weekly short code audits to identify violations, which include any deviations from
best practice and code of conduct guidelines, such as:
•
Missing links to Terms and Conditions or Privacy Policy webpages
•
Mandatory keywords (for example, STOP and HELP) aren’t displayed or nonfunctional
•
Failure to disclose that standard message and date rates may apply
•
Discrepancies between the short code's current use case and its originally approved program
The timely resolution of these audits is crucial, as failure to do so can result in short code suspension.
Make sure that you maintain compliance and promptly address any audit notices.
Best Practice and Compliance References
•
WMC Global Resources for the United States, including the CTIA Short Code Monitoring Handbook
•
Mobile Marketing Association U.S. Consumer Best Practices for Messaging

Messaging Considerations and Compliance
To improve your chances of receiving approval for your brand, campaign, and code requests, follow
237

=== PAGE 242 ===
Unified Messaging Unified Messaging Setup
these guidelines. Requests that don't meet these guidelines are likely to be rejected and could delay your
marketing efforts.
•
Include a valid business email address from your company’s domain in all requests. Using a free email
address such as Gmail or Outlook increases the likelihood of rejection.
•
Include your company’s physical address in all requests.
•
Include a functional website in your request that doesn’t include disallowed content in the content
you plan to send messages to.
•
Use content in your requests that is tailored to the audience you plan to send messages to.
•
Use accurate and specific content for all sample messages, opt-in requests, and opt-out requests.
Include as many sample messages as possible.
•
Fill out all fields in the brand, campaign, and code requests. Missing information delays the request
process.
•
If you allow opt-ins from physical media, such as billboards or flyers, include images of the media in
your request.
Long SMS Messages
When your SMS message gets a bit longer, we automatically split it into smaller segments to make sure it
delivers smoothly. To keep things efficient and easy for your recipients to read, we recommend keeping
plain text messages under five segments and Unicode (special character or emojis) messages under six
segments.
A2P 10DLC Messaging Throughput and Trust Score
To control spam, businesses must register their brands and campaigns before sending messages. In
response to registration, carriers raise message throughput rates based on the level of trust assigned to
the sender. 10DLC throughput rates are assigned based on trust score and campaign type.
•
Trust Score: A score from 0 to 100 is assigned by The Campaign Registry (TCR). Higher scores mean
higher message limits. To secure the best trust score, Salesforce recommends that you submit for full
brand vetting, even if you’re eligible for Sole Proprietor limits.
•
Campaign Type: The specific type of message such as customer support and marketing. All messages
must use a registered 10DLC campaign type matching the content's use case.
Carrier-Specific Limits and Rules
Throughput limits vary by carrier and campaign type. AT&T and Verizon Wireless queue messages that
exceed limits for later delivery, while T-Mobile and Sprint will result in an immediate hard failure
(messages are dropped). If your message fails with error code 4601, you’ve exceeded the daily message
limit. Don't resend the message within a 24-hour period; schedule it to be sent the next day.
238

=== PAGE 243 ===
Unified Messaging Unified Messaging Setup
AT&T and Verizon Wireless
Throughput is based on the campaign type or message class, and is measured per minute (TPM). AT&T
assigns throughput per campaign, not per brand. Each campaign is assigned a message class,
determining its specific throughput tier (TPM). Throughput applies to each campaign individually,
regardless of the number of assigned numbers, and isn't shared between campaigns under the same
brand.

Time.

Edge Cases and Minor Carriers Restrictions
Special use case: Throughput for charity use cases (K-12 Education) is fixed and isn't impacted by the
trust score.
Minor carriers: Throughput for US Cellular uses the standard major network rate, but is limited to 8
Messages Per Second (MPS). For all other minor US carriers such as Clearsky and others, the rate is fixed
at 1 MPS per phone number.
Sole Proprietor Limits
Sole proprietor brands (individuals or small businesses without a tax ID) are limited to 1 campaign and 1
phone number. Their fixed limits are:
•
Total MPS: 2.25 MPS for major US networks.
•
Daily Limit (T-Mobile): 1,000 messages per day.
•
Per-Minute Limit (AT&T): 15 messages per minute.

Describe how the opt-in experience for the subscriber takes place. If you use multiple opt-in methods,

notice that messaging and data rates may apply. Web opt-in requires an image of the URL or link. Verbal
opt-in requires a sample script.

information.

•

All Opt-Out Keywords and Confirmation Messages
Some keywords are included by default, such as STOP, QUIT, CANCEL, END, UNSUBSCRIBE, REVOKE,
and OPT OUT. You can add keywords that allow your subscribers to stop receiving messages. Any
subscriber who sends one of these keywords is removed from the campaign and receives no further
messages. The opt-out keyword response message sends when someone opts out. The text must include
the brand name and confirmation that no further messages will be sent.
All Help Keywords and Confirmation Messages
Some keywords are included by default, including HELP, that prompt the send of a help message when
received. You can also add keywords that allow your subscribers to receive help messages, such as INFO.
The help response message must have information to help subscribers or provide contact information
for assistance. This message must include a brand name and a point of contact, such as a URL, phone
number, or email address. You must also add opt-out language, frequency of messaging, and a notice
that message and data rates may apply. Canadian campaigns must include the French keywords ARRET
and AIDE. The INFO keyword must also include information in English and French.
Shared Terms, Conditions, and Privacy Policy URL
This link must include language indicating that the end user’s personal information won’t be shared or
sold to third parties for marketing purposes. You can’t hide consent for marketing messaging in shared
terms and conditions or privacy policies. SMS opt-in consent is never shared with third-party companies.
SMS consent can’t be purchased or shared from third-party companies. Consult with your company's
legal team to ensure your regulatory compliance.

SMS Engagement Data in Unified Messaging
Unified Messaging captures SMS engagement data in a data model object (DMO) in Data 360. Every
send or interaction with your SMS messaging activities generates this data. You can use these fields to
segment audiences or populate reports on your messaging activities.
Available in: Lightning Experience
Salesforce Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for Service Cloud AND Enterprise and Unlimited Editions
with Marketing Cloud Next Growth and Advanced Editions
Not supported in Government Cloud Plus
MessageEngagement DMO
This DMO contains information on eight different SMS engagement event types.
•
Sent - SMS message delivered to aggregator
•
Not_Sent - SMS message failed to arrive at aggregator
•
Subscribe - recipient opted in to receiving SMS messages
•
Unsubscribe - recipient opted out of receiving SMS messages
•
Confirmation - confirmation message sent to recipient regarding an opt-in or opt-out request
•
Help - recipient sent a message including a request for assistance using a specific help keyword
•
Click - recipient clicked a link sent in an SMS message
244

=== PAGE 249 ===
Unified Messaging Unified Messaging Setup
•
Undelivered - aggregator reports an error delivering the SMS message to a mobile number
All send types include this information.

with the event

Sample Use Case
After the events take place, you can use the data captured to create segments for use in sending targeted
messages. For example, you can create a segment of unified individuals based on who clicked links from
your messages at least three times in the past month. Segment on the EventDateTime value associated
with the Open event types, then collect the IndividualID values to determine who receives further
messages.
Pause Traffic in a Unified SMS Channel
To troubleshoot your channel configurations, pause your messaging traffic. You can pause all traffic to
the channel, or just pause sent or received messages via Flow and access to bots and human agents.
Available in: Lightning Experience
Salesforce Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for Service Cloud AND Enterprise and Unlimited Editions
with Marketing Cloud Next Growth and Advanced Editions
Not supported in Government Cloud Plus
247

=== PAGE 252 ===
Unified Messaging Unified Messaging Setup
11.. In Setup, in the Quick Find box, enter SMS Codes, and then select SMS Codes.
22.. Click the SMS code that you want to deactivate.
33.. Click Deactivate next to one or both applications.
44.. Save your changes.
When traffic is paused, SMS can’t be sent from or to the number in question. Agents and bots receive
errors if they try to send messages, and automated outbound or campaign messages aren’t delivered.
Agents can mark open messaging sessions as inactive if you intend to resume traffic within 48 hours. The
number is still associated with your channel in Salesforce, and it isn’t available for use in another channel
or with a different business service provider.
When you’re ready to resume traffic, activate the capabilities on the same page in Setup. After 48 hours
of paused traffic, all open sessions are ended. If traffic is resumed before 48 hours pass, agents and bots
can continue to handle their open sessions.
Activate and Deactivate SMS Channels
You can activate or deactivate Short Message Service (SMS) channels in your sandbox and production
orgs. However, the same SMS channel can't be activated in both orgs at the same time. SMS usage in the
sandbox or production org will deduct from your SMS credits. Before activating the SMS code in a
sandbox org, make sure that the code isn't being used in a production org.
Available in: Lightning Experience
Salesforce Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for Service Cloud AND Enterprise and Unlimited Editions
with Marketing Cloud Next Growth and Advanced Editions
Not supported in Government Cloud Plus
To activate or deactivae an SMS channels in your sandbox or production org.
11.. In Setup, in the Quick Find box, enter SMS Codes, and then select SMS Codes.
22.. Click the SMS code that you want to activate or deactivate.
33.. Click Activate for This Org to activate the SMS code if the code was deactivated. Or, click Deactivate
for This Org to deactivate the SMS code if it's already active.
The status changes to Activated for This Org or Deactivated for This Org based on the action you
selected.
Set Up an SMS Conversation in Unified Messaging

Then, you can route those replies to people or bots that can address them. To set up a conversation,
enable settings and create a flow.

Unified Messaging Consent
To send messages to your subscribers, you must have their explicit consent. You can’t transfer consent
from one Unified Messaging number or channel to another. You can set different required consent levels
for each application within a Unified Messaging number or channel. For example, in a unified SMS
channel used for both service and marketing, change the consent requirements of your marketing
interactions to require an explicit opt-in or double opt-in. You can manage how subscribers provide or
withdraw that consent within Unified Messaging.
RREEQQUUIIRREEDD EEDDIITTIIOONNSS
Available in: Lightning Experience
Unfied Messaging for Email and SMS is available in: Salesforce Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for
Service Cloud AND Enterprise and Unlimited Editions with Marketing Cloud Next Growth and
Advanced Editions
Unified Messaging for WhatsApp is available in: Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for Marketing Cloud
Engagement Growth and Advanced Editions
Not supported in Government Cloud Plus
Unified Messaging uses communication subscriptions to manage consent. Each SMS code or WhatsApp
channel number is mapped to one or more communication subscriptions. If a recipient opts in to a
Unified Messaging channel, they opt in to all of the communication subscriptions mapped to that
Unified Messaging channel. If a recipient opts out of a channel, they opt out of all communication
subscriptions mapped to that channel. See Understanding Consent Concepts in Marketing Cloud Next
and Considerations for Managing Consent Data
See Also
Manage SMS Consent
Inactive Unified Messaging Channels and Deprovisioning
Your Unified Messaging channel becomes inactive if your Salesforce Message Credits contract for that
channel expires, you cancel your Salesforce contract, your contract no longer includes Data 360, or you
250

=== PAGE 255 ===
Unified Messaging Billing Considerations for Unified Messaging
inactivate your Data 360 instance. When your channel is inactive, you can still review the configuration
and tracking information, but all send activities cease immediately. To reactivate your channel, contact
your Salesforce account executive.
Available in: Lightning Experience
Unified Messaging for Email and SMS is available in: Salesforce Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for
Service Cloud AND Enterprise and Unlimited Editions with Marketing Cloud Next Growth and
Advanced Editions
Unified Messaging for WhatsApp is available in: Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for Marketing Cloud
Engagement Growth and Advanced Editions
Not supported in Government Cloud Plus
After an account is inactive for 30 days due to an expired Salesforce Message Credits contract or 120
days because of an expired Salesforce or Data 360 contract, the channel is deprovisioned. The channel
data is queued for deletion, but your engagement data and billing and usage information remain as long
as you maintain an active Data 360 contract. All channel services (such as DKIM key retirement for email)
are fully deprovisioned at this time.
If not renewed, SMS codes also become inactive but remain under Salesforce management for 30 days.
After 30 days, all customer data (including operational and setup data and any applicable keywords) is
queued for deletion, and Salesforce stops maintaining the SMS code.
If your Data 360 instance is deleted, Unified Messaging no longer works. Creating a new Data 360 tenant
will not automatically restore Unified Messaging. To create the Data 360 tenant and restore Unified
Messaging, contact Salesforce Customer Support.
Billing Considerations for Unified Messaging
When you send a message, Unified Messaging uses both messaging services and Data 360 services. In
addition to Salesforce Message Credits, these activities also consume Data 360 credits.
Available in: Lightning Experience
Unified Messaging for email and SMS is available in: Salesforce Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for
Service Cloud AND Enterprise and Unlimited Editions with Marketing Cloud Next Growth and
Advanced Editions
Unified Messaging for WhatsApp is available in: Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for Marketing Cloud
Engagement Growth and Advanced Editions
Unified Messaging for email is supported in Government Cloud Plus
Unified Messaging for Mobile Apps is available in: Enterprise and Unlimited Editions for Marketing
Cloud Advanced Edition. Mobile App Messaging is available only in Marketing Cloud Next accounts
